RUSSIAN FEDERATION
GAS DISTRIBUTION COMPANY PRIVATIZATION STUDY
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE
INTRODUCTION
1.    The Ministry of Fuels and Energy of the Russian Federation has requested financing from the
World Bank to assist Rossgazifikazia in undertaking the next steps in privatization of the Gas Distribution
Companies (GDCs) in Russia.
OBJECTIVES
2.    The purpose of this study is to assist the Government in determining how to complete the
privatization process for the GDCs in Russia. The primary goals of the Government are the efficient
operation of these enterprises upon completion of this process and preservation of domestic interests in
the distribution of shares. In addition, the Government is interested in the contribution that can be made
to addressing the fiscal deficit through sales of shares.
BACKGROUND
3.    The first phase of the corporatization/privatization process for GDCs has been completed with
the formation of over 300 joint stock companies responsible for gas distribution in Russia. Under this
process, the employees of each GDC were given the option of owning 40 percent or 51 percent of the
shares, with the remainder owned by the Federal Government and local authorities. Most of the GDCs
established are profitable, with the exception being those with a relatively high proportion of residential
consumers. The financial situation of these companies will be addressed by further gas price increases
and through the establishment of a Gas Stabilization and Reconstruction Fund. This Fund will be
financed from a 10 percent charge on the differential between GDC purchasing and selling prices.
4.    The Government has requested the World Bank to finance a gas distribution reconstruction project
which is currently under preparation. This project will support the Government's initiatives in the gas
subsector and assist in the financing of gas distribution equipment identified as the result of a feasibility
study. This project will help GDCs become commercially oriented enterprises.
SCOPE OF WORK
5.    The consultant will review the operation of Volgograd Gorgas currently having JSC status as
candidates for privatization. The GDC's assets, staffing, managerial capabilities, operating policies and
financial health will be reviewed to determine a privatization plan. The consultant will recommend
specific actions that should take place prior to privatization.
6.    Task 1: Review the assets, operational and commercial policies and practices, management
capability, staff, and financial status of Volgograd Gorgas utilities. Identify key areas that are in need
of improvement and make specific recommendations regarding actions that should take place prior to
privatization.
7.    Task 2: Review optional sources for equity participation, including: (i) domestic capital markets;
(ii) existing shareholders; (iii) foreign equity participation, and describe the costs and benefits of each.



-87-
Annex 6-2
Page 13 of 24
8.    Task 3: Prepare alternative approaches to privatization for review by the shareholders. Present
the options to the shareholders, clearly identifying the next steps that need to be taken.
9.    Task 4: Assist the Government in preparing for the sale of their shares in the GDCs, taking into
account the Government's interest in receiving a fair value for their holdings.
REPORTING REQUIREMENT
10.   Upon the completion of each task, a report should be furnished to the Ministry of Fuels and
Energy, Rossgazifikazia, GKI, the GDCs and the Word Bank. Review meetings will take place in Russia
after the Task 2 and 3 reports are issued.



-88-
Annex 6-2
Page 14 of 24
RUSSIAN FEDERATION
GAS DISTRIBUTION REHABILITATION - PROJECT PREPARATION
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE
Introduction
I .    The Government of the Russian Federation (GOR) has requested the World Bank to finance a Gas
Distribution Rehabilitation Project (GDRP). In support of this project, the GOR has requested financing
of a study to undertake system diagnostics and project preparation for the proposed project. This study
will identify the highest priority investments that would enable Gas Distribution Companies (GDCs) to
meet the following objectives: (i) reduction of system losses, improved reliability and increased safety
of system operation; (ii) increased efficiency of customer energy use; (iii) transfer of technology and
design concepts; and (iv) commercialization of the gas distribution business. The project should be
prepared within the context of, and be consistent with, broader strategies for short and long term
development of the gas distribution industry.
Background
2.    Gas consumption, in Russia, amounted to about 420 Billion Cubic Meters (BCM) in 1991, of
which about 270 BCM (64 percent) is distributed by the distribution organizations that formerly
comprised RossGaz2 and are now in the process of being formed as Joint Stock Companies (JSC's).
Starting with intensive measures in the mid 1950s, the gas distribution industry has evolved to a position
where, by 1992, 218,000 km. of distribution pipelines supply 17.4 million households, 56,000
commercial consumers and 12,400 industries in 71 major distribution areas, with overall coordination by
RossGaz.
3.    Much of the distribution system suffers from corrosion-induced pipeline ruptures. Each year 300-
500 ruptures are caused by this problem. Insufficient cathodic protection and inadequate maintenance
due to insufficient supply of materials have been the primary sources of the problem. As a result,
Rossgaz estimates that 10,000 km of distribution pipelines are in need of replacement, of which 3,000
km is in urgent need of replacement or tubing with polyethylene (PE) pipes. A limited (5 km)
replacement program using PE pipes has been initiated on a pilot basis, which GDCs wish to accelerate.
4.    The role and structure of natural gas supply in meeting energy demands is likely to evolve
significantly in several areas over the next decade, including: (i) increased use of gas in power generation;
(ii) changes in the role of gas in household energy use and district heating; (iii) improvements in end-use
energy efficiency due to active energy efficiency efforts coupled with price rationalization and increased
use of metering; (iv) changing needs in the industrial and commercial sectors due to structural changes
in the economy; and (v) the impact of the use of new technologies. During 1993 the structure of the gas
distribution entities has changed considerably, with Rosstrojgazifikazia being split up into multiple
independent joint stock companies organized on the basis of oblast (or krai or republic) levels or city
levels.
5.    Gas use in households is largely limited to cooking, as hot water and space heating is mainly
supplied form a centralized district heating system. The current design of the district heating system is
2/The remainder is supplied by Gazprom (25 percent), MosGaz and LenGaz (5 percent each) in Moscow and
St. Petersburg, respectively.



-89-
Annex 6-2
Page 15 of 24
considered to be sub-optimal for many reasons, including high losses, inadequate controls, poor service,
and (implicitly) high costs of operation. Where district heating is economically efficient, the economic
prudence of gas service exclusively for cooking (as opposed to electricity-based stoves) is questionable.
Therefore, the relative role of district heating, electricity and gas use in households and commercial
buildings needs to be assessed before major investments in rehabilitation take place.
6.     The current system of energy delivery to households suffers from poor service. Space heating
is considered to be unreliable and inadequate.  Heating controls are virtually non-existent with
temperature largely controlled by opening windows. Stoves are reportedly also used to supplement the
inadequacy of heat delivery. Hot water supply is curtailed for about two weeks each summer while the
district heating system is taken out of service for repair. The scope for economically prudent increases
in energy use should be identified and a plan to address this issue should be developed.
7.     Longer term development of the gas distribution system will possibly include upgrading of the
existing low pressure steel network to a medium pressure PE based network to allow increased gas
demands to be met. A program of household metering will also be required. These needs and their
impacts must be assessed within the context of the overall demand for gas.
8.     The gas distribution industry is in the process of being privatized and adopting commercial
orientation. The first stage will occur during the first quarter of 1993 with full privatization starting in
1996. The ultimate structure of the industry is not yet finalized but the local distribution companies have
requested technical assistance to further develop commercial functions.
9.     Gas distribution companies will likely face cash flow limitations over the next 5 years and will
have limited access to foreign exchange. Rehabilitation solutions should therefore consider optimal use
of local goods and services.
10.    The Government has selected Volgograd Gorgas for their distribution rehabilitation efforts.
Study Objectives
11.   The consultant should prepare a work plan for comprehensive studies of a selected number of
cities. To enable the studies to be undertaken quickly, and because of the similarities in system design
among all cities, the consultant is encouraged to propose a structure to his work program that would
minimize duplication of effort. The study is designed to consist of three main elements: (i) demand
analysis; (ii) project preparation; and, (iii) institutional reform. The primary purpose of the study is to
quickly identify high rate of return, short gestation projects for each city that would be a component of
the long term gas distribution system development. In order that this objective is achieved, it is expected
that a team of foreign experts will work closely with a team of Russian counterparts to identify the
highest priority investments (both in terms of increased effectiveness of supply and increased end-use
efficiency). The study has four principle objectives - preparation of a gas distribution rehabilitation
project, increases in the efficiency of energy use, technology transfer and institutional reform - outlined
below.
12.   Prepare Distribution Network Reconstruction Project: Provision of reliable, low-cost gas to
Russian consumers requires investment in network reconstruction to reduce losses and improve safety.
The current gas distribution system is suspected of having relatively high losses due to pipe corrosion,
but the level of losses is unknown largely due to the lack of metering of gas consumption in households.
A technical audit of the distribution system to improve the estimate of current losses and the potential for



-90-
Annex 6-2
Page 16 of 24
savings from loss reduction and the development of a short term loss reduction program/strategy
consistent with the overall network rehabilitation program will be undertaken. The study will identify
a program of high priority distribution investments required over the next five years, along with
evaluation and preparation of specific projects in each city. This study and the resulting project will
provide critical inputs into the development of strategies for reconstruction of the gas distribution industry
over the next 5 years. The need for essential short-term investments should be balanced with the long-
term development of the network, based on consideration of strategic factors, some of which are outlined
below.
13.   Efficient Use of Energy: In comparison with norms in other countries, Russia's unit energy
consumption is unusually high. Drawing on earlier district heating and other related studies, the
consultant should review the scope for energy efficiency enhancements in a selected number of industries,
commercial enterprises and households to identify an investment strategy to improve the efficiency of gas
use. The objectives of the energy efficiency program would be to: free up gas for exports; reduce the
impact of gas price reform on downstream enterprises (and thus, the ability to pay); and reduce the
impact of energy use on the environment. For the housing stock, the consultant will prepare a design
competition to focus on three typical existing apartment complexes. The competition (which will be
prepared for financing under the proposed project) will focus on energy efficiency potential, and will also
address improvements in the quality of the housing stock. The consultant will identify a program of
technically and economically viable energy efficiency improvement measures and make specific
recommendations as to how to foster their implementation.
14.   Transfer of Technologv: The study will also introduce technologies used by the gas industry
outside of Russia, including, but not limited to: (i) distribution network design standards; (ii) the use of
different materials such as PE pipe; (iii) data acquisition and control technologies; and (iv) end-use
technologies.
15.   Institutional Reforn: The local distribution units are currently undergoing a major transformation
in corporate structure as a result of a decree signed by the President on December 8, 1992. RossGaz and
the GDCs have become joint-stock companies. This is the first step in a process of commercialization
that may eventually lead to full privatization. The consultant will review the institutional reforms
necessary to support this transfer of responsibilities and make specific recomnmendations on changes in
systems and procedures within each entity.
Scope of Work
16.   Based on the above background and objectives, the consultant is required to undertake this study
in three phases: (i) within the first three months, the consultant will prepare a diagnosis of the existing
situation to determine general changes in the role of gas in meeting energy needs and prepare a list of
short gestation, high return investments that will meet the immediate needs; (ii)one month after review
of the phase-one results by the GDCs and the World Bank, the consultant will prepare a project which
may be financed by the World Bank and/or other donors; and (iii) preparation of tender documents. The
major areas of investigation are outlined below.
Demand Analysis
17.   Gas Demand Forecast: Development of strategies for short and long term network reconstruction
and development will need to consider the implications of alternate levels of gas demand. Demand
scenarios should be developed with due consideration to the dynamics of the economy, changes in local



-91-
Annex 6-2
Page 17 of 24
economic structure including potential new investments, expected changes in gas consumption patterns
due to income and price changes, energy use, and a possible revised role for gas use in households. The
consultant should involve the local distribution company staff in the process of producing forecasts
including development of a simple end-use forecast model.
18.   Efficient Use of Energy: The potential for increases in energy efficiency should be assessed for
a diverse group of selected industries (about 8 per city) and commercial enterprises to determine cost-
effective investments and changes in operating practices that would reduce energy consumption. The
consultant should evaluate the achievable level of energy savings assuming gas price to industry is
adjusted to US$40/MCM equivalent. Energy audits for a selected number of enterprises in each city
should be undertaken. To the extent possible, efforts should focus on industries that are expected to
become or remain financially viable. The consultant should also examine alternate and innovative financial
and institutional means for funding such investments.
19.   Drawing on earlier district heating system and other related studies, the consultant will review
the overall provision of heating services to non-industrial customers and evaluate the costs and benefits
of changes which would improve the quality of services supplied. As a parallel exercise, the consultant
will prepare a design competition, to be included under the proposed project, which focusses on
apartment complex retrofit to improve building quality and reduce energy consumption. Designs for three
typical apartment complexes should be included as part of the competition.
20.   The Role of Gas: The consultant will evaluate the relative economic costs of heat and hot water
services from existing district heating versus residential gas boilers or electric boilers and stoves. This
will include an assessment of the long-term least-cost means of providing space heating, hot water and
cooking services to new and existing residential and commercial developments and evaluation of the
economically prudent geographic limit of existing district heating.
Project Preparation
21.    Asset Review: The state of distribution assets in place must first be evaluated to determine
priority investments, keeping in mind safety, loss reduction and environmental impacts. A maintenance
program for each city should be developed including corrosion protection, safety improvements, defect
monitoring, data acquisition and system control. The consultant should work closely with city distribution
staff in designing this program. This work would be complemented by visits of Russian staff to gas
distribution companies outside Russia.
22.   Specifically, the consultant should assess the present and forecast levels of system losses through
leakage in order that a priority investment program can be identified. The consultant will suggest a
program for undertaking this assessment. This analysis will be key in determining equipment to be
procured under the project. Cathodic protection should also be reviewed and recommendations, from the
system design perspective, should address this issue.
23.   Local Material Supply Capability: The consultant will provide an assessment of local supply
capability for potential goods and services required for the distribution network reconstruction project and
inform potential suppliers of the project and the requirements to participate in ICB bidding.
24.   Network Reconstruction and Development Strategies: Based on review of the existing network
configuration, the status of system losses and reliability and the future demand for gas, the consultant will
develop short and long term reconstruction and development strategies. An inventory of high priority



-92-
Annex 6-2
Page 18 of 24
investments for the next 5 years should be developed along with illustrative longer term investment
requirements. These recommendations should incorporate evaluation of existing design concepts and
standards relative to international practice and the scope for technology transfer. The consultant should
examine the costs and benefits of alternate design configurations including, but not limited to:
(i) maintain the use of the existing low pressure steel pipe system;
(ii) maintain the existing low pressure system but base expansion on medium pressure pipeline;
(iii) increase network capacity by phasing out the low pressure system, gradually replacing it with a
medium pressure network;
(iv) gradually substitute gas use in households, where it is only used for cooking, with electric stoves and
the cost effectiveness of alternate residential meter arrangements.
25.   Economic Analysis: The economic analysis will evaluate the least-cost development strategy of
energy supply, including an approximate estimate of the relative role of gas, electricity, and district
heating. The least-cost analysis will include both demand side and supply side investments. A ranking
of proposed investments for each of the cities will be established as an input to determining the highest
priority investments to be financed under the project proposed for World Bank financing. A specific
economic analysis of the highest priority investments for each city will be included to enable the
investments to be ranked.
26.   Project Preparation: Based on the results of a review of the proposed investments for each city,
the local distribution companies, the World Bank and the consultant will prepare the project, including
a detailed cost estimate (local and foreign costs in mid-1993 prices, local and foreign inflation, physical
contingencies, taxes and duties and interest during construction), contract packaging, implementation
schedule and proposed project management. After the broad scope of the project has been sanctioned
by the Executing Agencies and the World Bank, the consultant will assist the Executing Agencies to
prepare tender documents that meet World Bank guidelines.
27.   Environmental Analysis: An Environmental Assessment (EA) will be prepared for the proposed
project to ensure that the project meets the Environmental Guidelines of the Russian Federation, the
World Bank and those of local authorities. Attachment I provides a brief (non-exhaustive) guide to the
issues that should be addressed in the EA. The EA must be completed within four months of project
inception.
Institutional Reform
28.   Financial Analysis:  Based on pro-forma projections of the distribution company's Income
Statement, Balance Sheet and Sources and Application of Funds Statements for the years 1993 to 2003,
a financing plan should be developed by the consultants in close collaboration with the proposed
Executing Agency which would meet future funding requirements, including: the proposed high priority
investments, the longer term development program, on-going O&M expenditures and adequate levels of
working capital. The financial projections should be based on clearly identified targets for rate of return
on current valued assets, self-financing, liquidity, and capital structure that would satisfy potential
(private) investors and creditors. An estimate should be made of the margins and resulting natural gas
and LPG prices required to ensure financial viability. Local company staff should participate in the
analysis including development of a spreadsheet financial model.



-93-
Annex 6-2
Page 19 of 24
29.   As support for the process of corporatization and eventual privatization of the distribution
companies, the consultant will review the existing legal and regulatory framework which currently
governs the operations of the distribution companies and assess whether any administrative changes are
necessary to facilitate the transformation into joint-stock companies. The consultant will also review the
internal changes within the distribution companies that may be required as part of this change in status
including: the development of adequate systems of accountability to the shareholder, financial reporting,
organization structure, staffing and labor relations, billing procedures and systems, contracting services,
marketing and management information systems and make recommendations for development of these
practices, systems and staff. The consultant should identify current internal functions which would be
cost-effective candidates for eventual separation from the organization. The review should also contain
recommendations on what further legal or institutional changes may be required to prepare the joint-stock
company for transfer into private ownership. In addition, a diagnostic study of short term management
information requirements should be carried out. Cash management procedures (including receivable,
payable and inventory systems and strategies) should be examined in particular detail. The consultant
will identify critical areas where the distribution company would benefit from short term advisory services
and technical assistance and prepare terms of reference in conjunction with distribution company
management.
30.   The distribution companies will be required to maintain separate and auditable accounts for the
rehabilitation project with the goal of ensuring loan proceeds are utilized efficiently and for the intended
purposes. The contracted firm will assist the distribution company in enhancement of current project
accounting procedures and systems to ensure full accountability of project funds and enable timely
preparation of project progress and completion reports. The distribution companies will also be required
to prepare year-end financial statements according to both Russian standards and Generally Acceptable
Accounting Principles (GAAP). To support this the consultant will provide seminars on financial
accounting principles and practice and the adjusting entries required to transform Russian accounts to
basic international GAAP. Initial seminars should be directed at middle to senior management of the
distribution company with later seminars directed at specific accounting and economics functions in the
company.
31.   In preparation for financial audits the consultant (in conjunction with the asset review task
described in para 21) should assist the distribution companies to computerize their fixed asset register,
with due regard for materiality. All assets required for distribution operations, regardless of ownership,
should be included. This task should be carried out in consultation with the distribution companies
appointed auditors.
32.   Technology Transfer: Each city in the study will be twinned with a foreign distribution company.
Local staff, including one person from each of the following departments; (i) procurement; (ii)
accounting; (iii) maintenance; (iv) marketing and energy use; and (v) engineering, controls and safety,
will visit with counterpart staff for a period of approximately 6 weeks to learn about international
operating practices. They will be responsible for preparing logs and reports which will be presented upon
their return to Russia. There will likely be 2 or 3 study groups. The consultant will be responsible for
organizing the visits and should provide one person to coordinate the activities at each city. In addition,
a general manager from each Russian company will participate, who, in addition to learning about
international operating practices, should be exposed to the regulatory aspects of the local gas distributor,
the role of federal government agencies and the local and national Gas Associations.



-94-
Annex 6-2
Page 20 of 24
Scheduling and Reporting
33.   The consultant will report, in writing, to the GDCs and The World Bank: (i) upon the completion
of the identification of the priority projects; (ii) upon the completion of project preparation; and (iii) after
the completion of the tender documents. The consultant will work closely with the GDCs, maximizing
their participation in the diagnosis and project preparation in order to combine the best of foreign and
Russian technology.
34.   The consultant will submit eleven (11) copies of the first report to Rossgaz and the GDCs: (10)
in Russian and (1) in English; and ten (10) copies of the English version of the report to both and the
World Bank, within three months of the study inception. Based on the recommendations of this report
and subsequent discussions with the GDCs, RossGaz and the World Bank, the consultant will finalize
project preparation (including the EA) for a proposed World Bank project within one month of receiving
final directions from the GDCs and RossGaz in project definition.
35.   Upon the completion of project preparation, a draft final report will be submitted as described
above for the Phase I report. This report will form the basis of the World Bank appraisal of the proposed
project. Based on subsequent discussions with the GDCs and the World Bank, the consultant will assist
the GDCs staff to prepare tender documents in a manner which will satisfy World Bank guidelines.
Assistance to be Provided by the GDCs
36.   The GDCs will provide the following support services and facilities to the consultant without cost:
i)    assistance in obtaining visas, customs clearance, and any other administrative permits required
on behalf of the consultant in performing this assignment;
ii)    all relevant data, maps, surveys, studies, development plans, gas supply and similar information;
iii)   liaison with the Government of the Russian Federation, local government bodies, local
distribution companies and consumers;
iv)    estimates of the costs, availability and quantity of locally supplied materials, equipment, labor
and construction and installation services; and
(v)    a counterpart team for each group of cities to assist in the diagnostic and project preparation
components of the study.
Environmnental Aspects of the Proposed
Gas Distribution Rehabilitation Project
The Government of the Russian Federation requires that an Environmental Assessment (EA) be
undertaken for any significant gas distribution rehabilitation project as a component of an overall project
study. Furthermore, any gas project including a foreign exchange component in excess of 100 million
Roubles requires an EA satisfactory to the Ministry of Fuel and Energy, the local jurisdiction and be
approved by the State Environmental Commission in the Ministry of Ecology prior to initiating the
project.



-95-
Annex 6-2
Page 21 of 24
Most of the environmental legislation has only recently been put in place and, hence, the
experience in preparing EAs for gas distribution projects is limited. To assist in coordinating the
requirements and review by the various jurisdictions, the Ministry of Ecology has established an Inter-
Ministerial Coordinating Committee and a Center for International Projects designed to expedite projects
that have foreign investments. The Center is prepared to review the EA at the scoping and early draft
stage to identify any major deficiencies.
In order to help familiarize them with World Bank and Federal EA procedures,
Rosstrojgazifikazia has expressed their preference to employ consultants to assist them in preparing the
EA which will address the environmental standards of the Russian Federation and the World Bank. It
is understood that the Ecological Center of International Fuel and Energy enjoys the confidence of both
the Ministry of Fuel and Energy and the Ministry of Ecology.
The EA will describe the existing environment in the vicinity of the project and establish expected
environmental impacts associated with the undertaking. The environmental advantages and disadvantages
will be identified and alternatives in project design which may mitigate environmental problems will be
presented.
The EA will propose the details of the management of the identified impacts to minimize or
eliminate them and will set out mitigative and restorative measures that the owner will implement during
and after construction. The EA will set out a plan to monitor and report on the implementation of these
measures until the restoration has been successfully implemented.
The EA will address, as a minimum, the conservation of rare and endangered species, critical
habits, cultural properties, wetlands and significant environmentally sensitive areas. As well, the EA will
deal with the Occupational Health and Safety of the construction workforce in accordance with Russian
legislative and regulatory requirements. The handling and disposal of any hazardous materials associated
with the undertaking and the provisions to control and clean up any spills of hazardous materials will be
formulated in the EA.

Annex 6-2

RUSSIAN FEDERATION
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE - MOFE
The Development of a Gas Distribution Network Reconstruction Program till 2010
The Goals: The goals of this Study are to provide the Government with the services in the
selection of the facilities for the rehabilitation and improvement, in the clarification of its proper sequence
and financial sources.
The Current Status: There is an urgent need in the gas distribution networks rehabilitation.
Meanwhile the regional distribution institutions financial resources are limited. In these circumstances
it is important to define both the distribution networks that are in greatest need of attention and those
distribution companies which are able to implement the required reconstruction in most efficient way in
the current circumstances.
The Study Scope:  The Consultant will provide the analysis of the status of the majority of
distribution stock companies as being the potential participants of the Program. The technical conditions
of the distribution networks, the financial status of the companies, their management, industrial policy
will be evaluated from the point of view of the selection of the most efficient participants. The consultant
will propose the recommendation on the preparative measures till the reconstruction starts.
Task 1.  The analysis of the gas distribution networks technical conditions as well as of the
organizational, economical and financial conditions for the gas distribution systems reconstruction.
Task 2. The choice of the key aspects for the improvement and the preparation of the detailed
recommendations regarding the measures which should be realized till the distribution system
reconstructions.
Task 3. The preparation of the Russian gas distribution networks reconstruction draft program till the
year 2010 including the relevant assessment. This draft will be discussed with Rossgazifikazia, Ministry
of Fuel and Energy, regional authorities.
Task 4. The Consultant will finalize the draft program after observation by the Government and the
regional authorities have been taken into account.
The Study will address the measures that need to be taken by the Government in support of the
reconstruction Program. One of the major points to be addressed is to define the temporal and financial
scopes for the technical assistance of the international institutions in sector development, the means to
determine when and what should be on the distribution networks reconstruction, the potential for foreign
investments participation and the role of the companies own funds.
Tlhe Program has to cover the whole spectrum of the relevant problems including the stimulation
of the Russian production of the metering equipment, polyethylene pipes and other equipment.



-97-
Annex 6-2
Page 23 of 24
RUSSIAN FEDERATION
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE - MOFE
Development of the Legislation Specification to the Gas Supply
The Goals: The Study goals are to provide the government with the services in the development
of new legislation related to the gas sector and the provision of the regulation for the foreign investments
and financial support to it. The development of the legislative basis for the gas sector is a part of the
Governmental program of the economical reconstruction.
The Current Status: Regulation in the gas sector in Russia is evolving. The law "On the natural
resources" is adopted and the law "On the oil and gas" is under consideration. A decree on the regulation
of the gas industry was passed in December 1994. Meanwhile a number of existing Russian laws and
regulations need to be revised or called off as far as they create the obstacles to the gas sector effective
activity. As a result of the study the draft law "On the gas supply" as well as the proposals on the
correction of existing laws and regulations have to be developed.  The Study should assist the
Government in the policy implementation which will help to increase the efficiency in the growing gas
markets and to guarantee the rights and obligations for the gas producers and gas consumers.
The Study ScoDe: As a Study result the new legislative basis for the improved gas sector
efficiency in the developing market relations environment will be created. As expected, the Consultant
in order to achieve this goal, will implement the main tasks:
l.    The analysis of the current Russian legislative and regulative frame which forms the basis for the
business activities in the gas sector. The evaluation of the opportunities for the adaptation in the Russian
conditions the main legislative and regulative principles acting in the gas industry of the most
industrialized countries - as USA, Canada, UK, Germany, France, Norway, Netherlands, etc.
2.    The formation of the list of those new legislative acts which are required for the efficient gas
sector activity in the market conditions as well as of those legislative and regulative acts which should
be reviewed and corrected.  The discussions on the necessity and the directions of the desired
improvements in the legislation and regulations with the officials of the Ministry of Fuel and Energy,
Gazprom, Rossgazifikazia, gas producing and gas transporting enterprises.
3.    The development of the draft law "On gas supply" and on the proposals on the improvements in
the current legislation, with the contributions from the worldwide practice in this area. Among the main
subjects to be considered within this draft are: the licenses for the activities in the gas supply, the
supervision and controls on these activities, the operational procedures in the gas supply management,
the main requirements to the activities in the gas supply, the design and construction of the relevant
facilities, the state regulation in this area, the relationships between the gas suppliers, gas distributors and
gas producers, the involvement of the foreign investments, the responsibilities for the breach of this law
clauses, etc.
4.    The discussions on the draft law "On the gas supply" and on the proposals on the improvement
in the current legislation with the Ministry of Fuel and Energy, Gazprom, Rossgazifikazia and their
presentation before the Russian Government and Parliament.



-98-
Annex 6-2
Page 24 of 24
RUSSIAN FEDERATION
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE - MOFE
Coordination Function on Behalf of the Ministry as Between and Within Each Study
The Goals: To provide the Govermnent with the services in the management of the Study work
on each project in this group, for the analysis and acceptance of their results, as well as the provision of
the Russian side monitoring of the Study implementation.
The Scope of Services: This assistance is required in order to coordinate the study programs on
each individual project and to clarify the sequence of their implementation.
In practice all the technical assistance projects which support the main gas distribution
rehabilitation credit are interlinked. That is why it is necessary to correspond periodically the results on
each of them in order that their results and recommendations do not contradict each other. The
consultants have to clarify the needs of sectoral development and assist in the preparation of these
supplementary projects which would provide the opportunities for further realization of studies already
implemented. In some cases, it will be necessary to manage the joint review of the results of a number
of the interlinked projects. The preparation of such meetings, the formalization of its conclusions and
the due information of the relevant institutions and projects executors should be done by both Western
and Russian consultants. It would be required as well to organize the review of the interim and ultimate
studies results with the Fuel and Energy Ministry, other Governmnental institutions, Rossgazifikazia,
Gazprom, Regional authorities.

RUSSIAN FEDERATION
GAS DISTRIBUTION REHABILITATION AND ENERGY EFFICIENCY PROJECT
DRAFT IMPLEMENTATION PLAN
The implementation plan for the project reflects the capabilities and limitations of the participating
enterprises and agencies, in terms of the timing and scheduling of activities and the degree of assistance
required to ensure effective project implementation. It is designed to provide a realistic schedule for the
engineering, procurement, loan disbursement and installation of the project components based on the
Bank's prior experience in Russia and the relative inexperience of the participants in project
implementation. The balance of this Annex outlines the roles and responsibilities of the key personnel
involved in project implementation, a plan for initial project work, as well as the procurement plan and
the schedules for implementation of the project components. Annex 6-7 details the Bank's supervision
schedule, which is coordinated with key implementation milestones. Annex 6-6 details the project
monitoring and development indicators, which have also been coordinated with the anticipated
implementation schedule.
Gas Distribution Component
The network improvements component of the project will be implemented over four calendar
years, starting in the third quarter of 1995 through the second quarter of 1999. All components will be
launched in the first year of the project. A team will be formed to implement the project and will be
assigned staff with relevant background. A project director will head the team and be supported by
discipline coordinators. The key discipline coordinators required will be engineering, procurement,
planning and controls, construction and installation, quality assurance and administration. Considering
the high educational level of the GDC senior staff and their understanding of the problems faced by the
companies, the preferred option would be to assign senior staff to the project from within the GDC
organisation, with the chief engineer of the GDC taking the position of project director. The following
describes the principal responsibilities for the key personnel.
Project Director: The project director will have overall responsibility for the implementation of
the project. The director will report to the general manager of the GDC and have the following primary
objectives: i) to complete the project on schedule and within the agreed budget; ii) to ensure that the
quality, safety and environmental standards agreed for the project are understood and adhered to; iii) to
ensure that all documentation and reports are prepared on time and filed accordingly; and iv) to ensure
that the implementation team functions as an effective and cohesive group.
Engineering Coordinator: The engineering coordinator will have responsibility for all aspects of
the engineering including finalizing the technical specifications for procurement, completing the detailed
engineering required for the project and preparing detailed installation procedures, drawings, schedules
and plans. In addition the coordinator will work with the procurement group to finalize the commercial
sections of the bid packages, provide the basic input for the project schedules and regularly report the
completion status of the project tasks.
Procurement Coordinator: The procurement coordinator will be responsible for all aspects of
local and international procurement including issuing procurement notices, finalizing bid packages, issuing
bids, receiving proposals, supervising bid openings, evaluations and evaluation reports, preparing and
issuing purchase contracts. The responsibilities will also include coordinating with quality assurance on
vendor manufacturing surveillance, expediting and traffic control; arranging customs clearance and inland



-104-
Annex 6-4
Page 2 of 13
transportation where required; receiving inspection reports, warehousing and materials management after
delivery.  Regular reports will be prepared showing the status of all materials and equipment.
Planning and Controls Coordinator:    The planning and controls coordinator will be responsible
for all aspects of project planning, scheduling, cost estimating and cost control. The responsibilities will
include maintaining and updating the schedules and the cost estimate for completion of the project,
regularly analysing the project costs to ensure continued financial viability of the project and preparing
progress reports on the status of the project. Reports to the Bank on the financial aspects of the project
will be prepared in the standard Bank format. Regular discussions on the progress of the project will
be held with each coordinator and advice provided to the project director of potential cost or schedule
impacts.
Construction and Installation Coordinator: The construction and installation coordinator will be
responsible for all aspects relating to the construction and installation of the materials and equipment
associated with the project including preparing schedules and detailed procedures for the installation of
al] materials and equipment, coordinating the hiring of individuals or contractors for installation and
supervising the training of these personnel. During the installation period the coordinator would ensure
that quality, schedule and cost requirements are met and will provide regular reports to the project
director and the planning and controls coordinator.
Oualit Assurance (OA) Coordinator: The quality assurance coordinator will be responsible for
ensuring identifiable goals of quality are met throughout the project implementation. Reporting directly
to the general director of the GDC the QA coordinator will liaise directly with the project director on all
project quality related matters.  The responsibilities will include ensuring quality in the engineering,
procurement and installation of the materials and equipment, engaging 3rd party inspectors to carry out
inspections of foreign and locally supplied materials where required and coordinating all other material
inspections.  In addition the quality assurance coordinator will be responsible for ensuring safety is
maintained at all times on the worksite and also that the environmental mitigation measures are effectively
carried out.
Administration Coordinator: The administration coordinator will be responsible for all aspects
of office administration including office space coordination, secretarial services, office equipment
coordination, project filing system development and maintenance and project document control.
Note: It should be noted that all the coordinators described above may not necessarily be
dedicated full time to work on the implementation of this project. For example the planning and controls
coordinator could come from the existing accounting department and may have other responsibilities also.
Similarly the quality assurance coordinator may be responsible for quality throughout the GDC. On the
other hand coordinators such as the engineering, procurement  and construction and installation
coordinators will be dedicated full time to the project and each may have several people working for
them.
Technical Assistance to the GDC: Considering the GDC's lack of experience with international
and Bank procedures, especially with regard to finance and procurement, it is proposed that consultant
support services be provided under the proposed loan. The selected consultants should be conversant
with both Russian and Bank practices and should have the backing or support capabilities to carry out
their work effectively.  It is expected that the consultants will travel to, and remain in, Volgograd
working with the implementation team on an as required basis. The consulting teamn will include the
following skill mix:



-105-
Annex 64
Page 3 of 13
(a)    Two consultants specializing in gas distribution will support the technical areas: the first, a gas
distribution specialist, with expertise in design and implementation of all aspects of gas distribution
networks will provide advice on project implementation to the project director and the technical groups.
The other, a gas metering design specialist, with expertise in metering design and specification, will be
required on a short-term basis only to assist the engineering group.
(b)    A  procurement specialist will advise the procurement group in all aspects of the procurement
process and also will recommend institutional changes to strengthen the GDC's capability to procure from
local sources and abroad.
(c)    A financial analyst will assist the planning and controls group and the GDC financial managers
in establishing project accounting procedures, in facilitating the preparation of financial statements that
conform to international standards, and in providing general financial advice to the GDCs.
(d)    An independent 3rd party inspection company will be engaged to provide factory inspections for
materials and equipment.  As most of the equipment is standard and not engineered products the
requirement for this service is expected to be small.
In view of the urgency, it is proposed that requests for proposals for consultants under (a), (b)
and (c) above be issued as soon as loan negotiations have been concluded. The cost of the specialists
is estimated at US$1.5 million. The twinning arrangements proposed under the technical assistance
component of the project would complement the activities of the consultants. In view of the timing and
the fact that the utilities executing the twinning arrangements may also lack experience in Bank
procedures, the twinning is not seen, however, as a substitute for technical assistance.
In addition to the technical assistance financed by the Bank the GDCs may require assistance from
local consultants in the following areas:
(a)    A local procurement agent may be required to provide assistance in such areas as local
procurement, customs clearance for inported materials and local transportation of materials.
(b)    Assistance from a local engineering institute may be required to prepare the detailed installation
procedures and drawings as these institutes have been doing this work in the past.
Energy Efficiency Component
RESF would be responsible for evaluating, overseeing, and administering onlending for the
energy efficiency components of the project. During the first year, the energy efficiency projects will
be restricted to three of the four cities visited during appraisal (Volgograd, Ryazan and Saratov) plus St
Petersburg. In the following year, the geographic scope will be extended to include Nizhni-Novgorod,
Samara, Rostov-on-the-Don, Stavropol, and Vladimir. Pending the findings of a mid-term review, limits
on the geographic scope of the project could be lifted for the remaining years and for projects financed
through reflows.
The responsibilities of RESF will include: (a) the review and approval of detailed sub-project
procurement needs (prepared by the district heating companies and local power plants); (b) review and
approval of the execution plan for procurement activities, review of the economic and financial rates of
return and of the financial viability of the borrower; (c) control and review of the technical and financial



-106-
Annex 6-4
Page 4 of 13
aspects of sub-project implementation; and (d) review of the environmental assessment of the sub-
projects. Based on their review, the RESF staff will submit qualifying sub-projects to a loan review
committee, which will include the agency's board, supplemented by representation from the Ministry of
Finance. The review committee will be authorized to approve projects requiring loans up to US$1
million. Projects requiring loans of more than US$1 million, as well as the first two projects in each
service area, will be submitted to the Bank for final review and approval. A separate group will be
established within the RESF to implement the energy efficiency component of the project. During the
initial phases of the project, RESF will be assisted in both project evaluation and implementation by
consultants to be financed under the institution strengthening component of technical assistance.
Two sources of financing will be made available under the project to assist RESF: (a) the spread
between the Bank lending rate and the onlending rate will include 0.5 percent to cover their administrative
costs; and, (b) part of the proposed GEF project on greenhouse gas reduction will be used to finance the
costs of establishing this unit. It is proposed that the debt servicing payments by the executing agencies
be made as two separate components - one of 0.5 percent to RESF and the other to the Government,
excluding the 0.5 percent spread designed to cover RESF's administrative costs. This would provide an
incentive for RESF to undertake an effective follow-up on repayments. The RESF will submit cash flow
and income statements on a quarterly basis, detailing how their income was spent. Ministry of Finance
will be responsible for managing repayment of the subsidiary loans. The advisability of their contracting
this task to an agency bank will be discussed during negotiations.
The primary criteria for the viability of sub-projects will be: (a) an economic rate of return of
not less than 20 percent (real); (b) a financial rate of return of not less than 10 percent (real); (c) a
demonstrated ability on the part of the ultimate borrower to finance the local portion of project costs from
internally generated funds; (d) the technical feasibility of the proposal; (e) the proposed implementation
plan; (f) a debt service ratio of at least 1.2 to demonstrate the ability, on the part of the borrower, to
repay the loan to the Ministry of Finance; and, (g) an environmental assessment which meets Russian
requirements.
Technical Assistance Component
The components of the technical assistance related to project implementation, that is, the
assistance to the project implementation teams in the GDC and the training and technical support to the
RESF, will be implemented by the beneficiary agencies. The studies proposed for financing under the
loan will be implemented by the Department for Gasification and Gas Industry of the MOFE. The
proposed technical assistance includes a component for assistance to the MOFE in overall study co-
ordination, which will provide support to the ministry's implementation efforts. It has also been proposed
that the MOFE delegate implementation responsibility for the study to upgrade and internationalize the
technical gas standards and procedures to Rossgazifikazia, based on the latter's skills and interests in this
subject.
Implementation Schedules
Gas Distribution Component: The draft schedule for the implementation process is shown on
pages 6 and 7 of this Annex. This schedule outlines the activities which must be started in the first year
of implementation.  Implementation of the project was advanced during the Loan negotiations by
reviewing draft tender documents.  The first activity will be the selection of consultants for
implementation assistance. The Terms of Reference and Letter of Invitation has been finalized and will



-107-
Annex 6-4
Page 5 of 13
be issued as soon as possible so that a contract can be signed and the selected consultanms can mobilise
shortly after the loan is made effective. At the same time the procurement process for materials and
equipment has been initiated with the drafting of a General Procurement Notice. The technical
specifications and bidding documents need to be finalised so that tenders can be issued shortly after the
loan is made effective and the consultants for implementation assistance are mobilised.  (Note: Draft
Technical Specifications and TOR for consultants have been prepared during project preparation). Issue
of the tender documents in the third quarter of 1995 is essential if contracts are to be awarded and
disbursements made in 1996. The other activity which must start soon after negotiation is the
determination of exactly how much engineering work is required by the GDC, how will that work be
carried out and arranging the resources to carry out the engineering. In addition the GDCs must start
the detailed planning of how the construction and installation of the materials and equipment will take
place.
Summary schedules for the components are shown on pages 8 through 10 and the Procurement Plan and
Schedule on Page 1l. These schedules show that the major components of meters, cathodic protection
and SCADA would require 3 to 4 years to be fully implemented.  More detailed schedules for each
component will be required as implementation progresses.  These will be prepared by the project
implementation teams within the first 6 months of the project.
Technical Assistance and Energv Efficiency Components: Page 1 1 shows the planned schedule
for implementation of the technical assistance components of the project. All of the Technical Assistance
items will be started in the first year of implementation. Finally, page 12 shows the proposed schedule
for the initial phases of implementation of the energy efficiency component. Beyond the initial phases,
however, the schedule will depend on the rate at which qualifying subprojects are submitted for appraisal
to the RESF.

RUSSIAN FEDERATION
GAS DISTRIBUTION REHABILITATION AND ENERGY EFFICIENCY PROJECT
ENVIRONMENTAL MITIGATION PLAN
1.    The Bank has determined that this project requires a "category B" Environmental Mitigation Plan
(EMP), as defined in the Bank's Operational Directive on Environmental Assessment, O.D. 4.01.
2.    The Russian Federation environmental requirements are outlined in the Environmental Assessment
Manual, 1992, which implements RSFSR Law on Environmental Protection, no. 2060-1, adopted
December 19, 1991. According to RSFSR Law on Environmental Protection No. 2060-1, adopted 19
December, 1991, Section V, Articles 36, 37, and Section VI, Articles 40,42 and 43, and Environmental
Assessment is required for this project under the category of "rebuilding of facilities." According to the
Environmental Assessment Manual, updated in 1992, ecological and other related implications of a project
must be considered in "remodeling or technically refurbishing" facilities. An EMP is also required if
foreign equipment is introduced. The environmental analysis is subject to review by the Ministry of
Environment and Natural Resources.
3.    After approval of the loan, site specific engineering will be undertaken in order to determine
parameters of each project. The engineering phase will result in recommendations for locations of pipe
replacement and specific amounts of pipe to be replaced. Locations for implementation of cathodic
protection will be determined after new leak detection equipment is in place and a survey of the system
has been completed. Specifications for the SCADA system will be developed, required RTU and meters
for the industrial and commercial customers will be identified and suppliers selected after evaluation of
competitive bids is completed.
4.    The engineering phase will also result in development of specifications for installations of burners,
controls, BTU meters, control values for district heating systems and district heating plant modifications,
and specifications of similar equipment as well as heat recovery systems for the industrial plant energy
conservation projects.
5.    Subsequent EMPs will be prepared by each of the three cities on the specific gas distribution
system projects. These EMPs will be reviewed by the Ministry of Fuel and Energy and the Ministry of
the Environment and Natural Resources and by other agencies as appropriate.
6.    During preparation of the EMP, discussions took place with representatives of the Environmental
Committees and occupational safety officials in the three cities as well as representatives of the Ministry
of Fuel and Energy and the Ministry of the Environment and Natural Resources. Their interests and
concerns were incorporated in the EMP.
7.    The beneficial impacts of the project include reduced methane leak potential and potential for gas
conservation. These are discussed in greater detail below.
8.    Reduced Methane Leak Potential: Replacement of deteriorated pipes, installations of a cathodic
protection system and new testing equipment will reduce the potential of gas leaks and result in two
impacts:
*     Increase in public safety by reducing the risk of explosion due to undetected leaks;



-117-
Annex 6-5
Page 2 of 5
*     A cumulative beneficial impact resulting from the reduced potential for release of methane to the
atmosphere, thus reducing the greenhouse effect. Since methane emissions produce a greenhouse
signal that is 20 to 50 times greater than carbon dioxide for equivalent emissions, it is the second
most significant greenhouse gas being emitted by man's activities.
9.    Potential for Gas Conservation: Increased efficiency in the delivery of gas through the reduction
in the potential for leaks, through pipe replacement, cathodic protection and new testing equipment, better
system controls through installation of SCADA, and the combination of upgrading and new metering and
a change in pricing policy will result in gas conservation. This will make more natural gas available to
accommodate future population growth. As market forces create a greater external demand for gas at
higher prices, increased sales made possible by conservation of gas will result in an increase in an
economic benefit to the Russian economy.
10.   As a result of implementing the gas conservation projects (district heating and industrial plants),
the total yearly emissions of NOx. would be reduced by 1,064 tons and C02 emissions would be reduced
by 83,621 tons. These are considered to be beneficial projects.
11.   The potential adverse impacts of the project are the following:
-     Construction Impacts--Pipeline replacement will result in short term construction related impacts.
This will include traffic circulation, air quality, odor, soil erosion, water quality, fish movement,
noise and public safety risks.
-     Traffic Circulation and Other Public Activities--a potential temporary disruption of traffic
movement.
-     Air Quality--dust during clearing and grading activities, during trench digging and while moving
soil.
-     Odor--gas venting will result in odor near blowdown sites. The duration of detectable odor in
these cases is usually from a few minutes to an hour.
-     Soil erosion-in hilly areas there would be a potential for increase in soil erosion as a result of
the pipe replacement activities.
-     Water quality--if oil degraded pipes are not removed and disposed of properly at river crossings,
this could result in degradation of water quality.
-     Barrier to Fish Movement-trenching in the rivers may result in a temporary barrier to fish
movement.
-     Construction Noise-trucks, bulldozers, and welding equipment will be required for grading,
trenching, pipe laying, and back-filling. These pieces of equipment produce noise levels of 70-85
dBA at a distance of about 50 feet.
-     Increased Public Safety Risks-the old pipes that will be removed will be purged of gas and then
removed. There is a potential for public safety risks from normal construction operations.
12.   Mitigation measures that need to be taken are the following:



-118-
Annex 6-5
Page 3 of 5
a)    Construction Mitigation Measures for Pipe Replacement-- Protection of other Utilities--prior to
construction, the location of other utilities underground and above ground in the vicinity of the pipe must
be identified and permits from local authorities obtained. During construction, all the other utility lines
must be protected. Each utility should remain in full operation during construction. All ditches must
be returned to their original condition or better.
b)     Construction Safety-- In addition to the World Bank Occupational Health and Safety Guidelines,
Russian Federation Requirements will be adhered to as follows:
*  Instructions of SNiP 2.04.08-87: "Gas Supply" and "Safety Rules for Maintenance of Gas
Utilities ";
*  Russian Federation Health and Safety Regulations in the Gas Industry, 20 October, 1991;
*  Norms for Safety in Construction Industry, 1991;
*  Safety Rules and Norms in the Construction Industry. Noise Protection, July 1, 1978;
*  Federal Standard GOST 12.1.003-83
*  SNiP 2.05.06-85, Section 9, Environmental Protection for Pipelines;
*  SNiP 3.05.02-88, Building Code Gas Supply;
*  The State Committee for Safe Performance Supervision in Industrial and Mining Sectors, Safety
Rules in Gas Industry;
*  GosGor TechNadzor, Safe Operation of Reservoirs which are under pressure;
3  RosStroysGas, Operations, Regulations in Gas Industry, Health and Safety Regulations, July 1,
1992.
Each city has its own occupational safety regulations. Construction procedures should be in conformance
with all city regulations that apply.
c) Construction Procedures:
* Research of Pipelines--no excavation should be undertaken until detailed research of the existing
underground structures is completed by a qualified pipeline engineering concern.
* Pot holing--pot holing is the advance digging by hand to locate underground structures. Pot
holing should be used whenever it is necessary to locate the position of underground structures.
* Protection of Existing Drainage Patterns-at stream or river crossings, new pipeline should be
buried at least 3 meters under the scour line.
* Erosion control--in hilly areas where there is a potential for erosion, an erosion control plan
should be prepared.
* Dust Control--the construction area should be sprayed with water to control dust.
* Construction Noise--prior to venting of gas as part of pipe replacement operations notice should
be given to surrounding area residents and commercial and industrial establishments. Construction
activities should take place only during the daytime, and should conform to city noise ordinances and
regulations, as applicable.
* Treatment of Removed Old Pipes--the old pipes that will be removed should be purged of all gas
and then removed. Pipes that are abandoned in place should be cut, capped, and filled with inert



-119-
Annex 6-5
Page 4 of 5
nitrogen gas to eliminate future risks.
* Water Quality--the hydrostatic test water should be drawn from nearby sources, pressurized in
the pipe, tested for contamination, and then discharged to an existing waterway.
* Solid Waste-all solid waste generated at the construction site should be removed from the site
and deposited at an approved solid waste disposal facility.
* Toxic Soil--The potential for the presence of toxic materials in the soil should be investigated
prior to construction, and construction activities should be carried out according to the best practices
of health and environmental safety.
* Construction Inspectors--the gas utility in each city should designate inspectors to perform regular
inspections of construction activities to ensure that the contractors are following proper construction
procedures.
e Fire Protection and Emergency Response-an emergency response should be prepared for the
project prior to construction.
3 Continuation of Vehicular Circulation--vehicular circulation should not be disrupted during
construction.
* Vehicular Safety During Construction on the Road and on the Construction Site--all Federal and
local laws dealing with vehicle safety during construction should be adhered to.
* Future Maintenance--future maintenance activities should be undertaken on a regular basis as
follows:
* Periodic checks of cathodic protection equipment to ensure proper operation and effectiveness of
corrosion protection; maintain active participation by other agencies to ensure that notice is given
by them prior to excavating in the vicinity of the gas system pipe; leak surveys; maintenance of
valves, regulators, and metering devices according to regular schedule.
Mitigating Measures Monitoring:
a)    Public involvement during project implementation should be conducted as part of the project for
the residential and the commercial establishments that would be affected by the short term construction
impacts of the project.
b)    Monitoring of the implementation of mitigation measures should occur before, during and after
the pipe replacement has taken place. Monitoring should encompass all the mitigation measures required
as conditions of the project to ensure that they have been properly executed. Monitoring should be the
responsibility of the Environmental Coordinator.
In order to ensure that the project mitigation plan is executed effectively, the environmental management
capability of Volgograd Gorgas should be enhanced. Organizational changes should be instituted as
follows:
* A new position of Environmental Coordinator should be established within each gas utility



-120-
Annex 6-5
Page 5 of 5
company.
*  A staff development program for environmental compliance should be instituted
* Technical Assistance Program designed to keep the newly appointed Environmental Coordinator
current with developments in the environmental field
* Equipment Support for Environmental Management to support the environmental coordinator and
the personnel in the Environmental Committees. Various types of equipment should be supplied
to assist them in their work. Equipment considered are computers, including environmental and
gas distribution standards and procedures translated into Russian, fax machines, noise meters, and
air filters.
c)    Implementation responsibilities of the training program will be the responsibility of the GDC.
Areas of training would include:
m A counterpart coordinator will be designated in the foreign GDC to supervise training activities
there. This coordinator will be responsible for implementation of the program as planned. Each
trainee will have a mentor for the duration of the training. The mentor will be responsible for
follow-up, guidance, and support to the trainee while he/she is abroad.
* One person will be designated for training. This person will spend a total of three months
abroad. The first month will be spent during the engineering phase, in the first 6 months of the
project. The second month will be spent just prior to start of construction. The third month will be
spent after construction is completed.
Cost mitigation strategies are as follows:
a)    No additional costs are expected for construction mitigation measures because the best engineering
and construction practices would incorporate all of the measures recommended above as part of the
project cost. The cost of the public involvement program would be included in the project specific EMPs
to be prepared at a later phase.
b)    The total cost of the mitigation program would be $205,000, consisting of about $40,000 per year
for the environmental management program, $115,000 for the environmental training program, and
$50,000 for equipment.

ENERGY EFFICIENCY PROJECT
DEVELOPMENT INDICATORS
During project implementation a number of key indicators will be reviewed to ensure that the
project's objectives are explicitly monitored and controlled. The key areas of concem under the project
are that: (i) the financial viability of the borrowing enterprise is maintained; (ii) projected energy savings
take place; (iii) access to information increases to enable improved network design; and, (iv) project costs
are minimized. The following outlines the key variables that will be assessed and how the information
will be dealt with which are summarized in the table below.
Monitorable Targets
1996       1997       1998       1999
Gas Distribution Component (cumulative)

Financial Performance (annual)
Self-Financing Ratio                  20%        30%        30%         30%
Return on Revalued Assets             10%        10%         10%        10%
Debt Service Ratio                     1.5        1.5        1.5        1.5
Accounts Receivable (sales equivalent)  3 mo.    3 mo.      3 mo.      3 mo.
Financial Viability
The key areas of concern regarding financial viability of the enterprises relate to self-financing
capability, debt servicing capability and the level of accounts receivable relative to sales.



-122-
Annex 6-6
Page 2 of 2
Each October, the utility will furnish a budget for the next fiscal year, indicating how the
proposed self-financing ratio covenant will be met to ensure that local costs can be financed from
internally generated funds. The analysis will focus on prices and production costs to ensure that
appropriate actions are taken to meet the project objectives.
Within three months of the end of each fiscal year, Volgograd Gorgas will furnish a copy of its
audited financial statements to the Bank for review. This review will focus on the profitability of the
enterprise and ensure that no new debt is undertaken that would undermine its debt service capability.
It will also focus on the return to shareholder's capital, so that the transition to a successful independent
joint stock company can be realized.
The accounts receivable situation is the current primary concern in the energy sector. Hence,
monthly summaries (which would later become quarterly summaries once they have been proven to be
successfully dealt with) of the status of this variable will be reviewed. Specific actions on debt swaps
and cutting-back/off supply to non-payers will be reviewed during supervision missions.
Energy Savings
The project includes two components that are expected to result in energy savings - induced
reduction of gas use from metering and investments in equipment that will decrease energy consumption.
The reported gas savings from similar metering projects in Russia has ranged from 25 to 50 percent.
Therefore, data will be collected on gas consumption during the early stages of meter implementation to
establish baseline data. Monthly records will then be kept for a period of about two years (to establish
the effect of seasonality on consumption) to determine the impact of metering on household gas
consumption.
Investments in energy savings (burners, controls, boilers) will be assessed to determine the impact
of these investments on energy efficiency. If some of these investments are shown to have particularly
high impacts, RESF will attempt to have similar investments implemented in other cities.
Access to Information
Under the gas distribution rehabilitation component, the GDC will have improved access to
information as a result of the SCADA system. The combination of this information and network analysis
tools is expected to enable their staff to better design investments in system upgrades. The leak detection
equipment will also provide better information on fugitive methane emissions. This information, coupled
with the implementation of cathodic protection, will enable the GDC staff to identify problem areas in
their network which need to be addressed. This information will be collected to determine the best way
in which the cathodic protection system should be implemented and will enable the GDCs to assign
priorities for pipe replacement.
Project Costs
Uncertainties with respect to project costs will be explicitly dealt with during project
implementation. One of the key questions that will be addressed is the ability of Russian suppliers to
compete under Bank-financed ICB. If barriers to entry are identified, an assessment of these barriers will
be undertaken to determine how they might be overcome.

ECONOMIC ANALYSIS
ASSUMPTIONS
A.    Project Costs
1.    Cost estimates and the timing of the costs for the Control and Asset preservation and Metering
components and the timing of these are based on the cost estimated, as shown on page 3. The cost
estimate for the Efficiency component is based on consultant estimates.  The timing of the costs for the
efficiency component are assumed to be divided 30, 40 and 30 percent in 1996, 1997 and 1998
respectively.
2.     Environmental costs are included in the control and asset preservation component. Costs for an
environmental coordinator position in each city is are included as well as a training component. The
estimate also includes equipment to enhance the environmental capability of the utility in each city. The
total costs are US$141,000 in year 1, US$66,000 in year 2 and US$20,000 thereafter.
B.    Project Benefits
Control and asset preservation component:
-     Extension of pipeline lifetime from 20 years to 60 years:
- Replacement cost of buried pipelines: US$114/m. The timing of the benefits is pro-rated
in accordance with cumulative capital costs incurred, including a one-year lag function.
-     Power savings - Economic value: US$0.065/KWh.
-      Savings related to network analysis and control - 10 percent increase in benefits obtained
through extended pipeline life.
Efficiency Component
4.    The sum of gas savings in each project, as estimated by the consultant. The timing of the
benefits is pro-rated in accordance with cumulative capital costs incurred, including a one-year lag
function.
- Economic value: US$40/MCM
Metering Component
5.     Gas savings:
- Industrial meters: 2 percent of gas consumption
- Apartment blocks, private space heating and commercial customers: 25 percent of
consumption. The timing of the benefits is pro-rated in accordance with cumulative capital



Annex 7-1
Page 2 of 6
costs incurred, including a one-year lag function.
Economic value:
- Industrial customers: US$40/MCM.
- Commercial, apartment blocks, private space heating: US$140/MCM
